## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / batch reactor dynamics)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of concentration A(t), which is the standard dependent variable in chemical kinetics ODE models. With only t and A available, the most common relationships are empirical/mechanistic rate laws where dA_dt depends on A (reaction order, autocatalysis, reversibility) and sometimes explicitly on t (time-varying rate constants due to temperature programs, catalyst deactivation, illumination changes, etc.).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (A decreases linearly in time when rate is concentration-independent)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay; many elementary decompositions)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular with identical reactant or pseudo-second-order regimes)
- nth-order (power-law) kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order for non-elementary mechanisms)
- Source–sink (CSTR-like or production + decay): dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (net formation at constant rate with first-order loss; also linearized kinetics near steady state)
- Linear relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1; reversible or buffered systems)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous unimolecular and bimolecular consumption channels)
- Autocatalytic / logistic-type rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-accelerating growth with depletion/limit; common in autocatalysis and some polymerization models)
- General polynomial rate law: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (local model for complex mechanisms or truncated series expansion)
- Time-varying first-order (exponential acceleration/deceleration): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant changes exponentially with time, e.g., catalyst activation/deactivation)
- Time-varying first-order (linear drift): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * t) * A (rate constant drifts due to slow condition changes over experiment duration)
- Time-modulated source term: dA_dt = c0 * exp(-c1 * t) - c2 * A (decaying feed/illumination-driven production with first-order loss)
- Explicit time-polynomial forcing: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * t + c2 * A (non-stationary environment or ramped input affecting net rate)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA_dt is consistently negative and roughly proportional to A, it indicates first-order consumption; log(A) vs t tends to be linear in the underlying solution.
- If dA_dt magnitude scales with A**2 (strong curvature; faster drop at higher A), it suggests bimolecular/second-order kinetics.
- A nonzero intercept term in dA_dt at A≈0 (dA_dt ≈ -c0 or +c0) signals zeroth-order loss or a constant source term (e.g., inflow, constant generation).
- A factor (A - c1) indicates relaxation toward an equilibrium level c1; sign changes around A=c1 imply stable fixed point behavior typical of reversible/feedback-regulated systems.
- Presence of multiple powers (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2) suggests parallel reaction pathways or regime mixing (one pathway dominates at low A, another at high A).
- A*(c1 - A) structure indicates autocatalysis with self-limitation; dA_dt changes sign at A=0 and A=c1, giving two fixed points and sigmoidal time courses in A(t).
- Explicit exp(c*t) factors multiplying A imply time-varying rate constants; this is consistent with catalyst deactivation/activation, aging, or time-programmed conditions.
- Linear or polynomial dependence on t in coefficients (e.g., (1+c1*t)*A or +c1*t) suggests slow drifts, ramps, or unmodeled experimental trends rather than purely concentration-controlled kinetics.
- Non-integer reaction order in A**c1 (c1 not near 1 or 2) often points to empirical/global kinetics, transport limitations, or composite mechanisms rather than a single elementary step.
